< review>
I really want to love this place but I can't. Time and again the customer service experience leaves a lot to be desired. Today I ordered by way of
Postmates using Google Maps. Order was marked ready within 12 minutes. Arrived 20 minutes later to learn they were out of items I ordered and so they requested I order something else.  So I did. Waited another 20 minutes, got my take out and left. When I got home and saw how small the $18 entree was disappointment ensued. The food, yes, is delicious however the prices are ridiculous - even for LA.

This is probably my 10th visit to Camp Pho. I was a frequent and forgiving customer in their opening days. Regretfully 3 years later I can't say much has changed as in the way of customer experience. The staff are really nice yet somehow a systematic approach to having a quality restaurant experience doesnt seem to work here.< /review>

< Text>
Complete rip-off. We ordered from Postmates and the poor driver had to wait for 50 minutes until the order was ready (it's pre-made broth and then you toss some ingredients in a bowl, how can that take so long?). After our food arrived over an hour late and cold, we were in shock to see that a Pho bowl of $18 was a mini size. We ordered two large ones and both of them were tiny. The broth wasn't even enough to cover the noodles. I order pho a lot and will never choose Camp again - you get triple the size for half the price elsewhere. The taste was great but what good does it do when you're still hungry after an order over $40.< /Text>

<userid>109770455507879479188<//userid><rate>1< /rate>< review>
2 Words: All Hype.

Camp Pho started off as an In-Tents(ha!) food adventure and quickly turned out to be a wet Tee-pee.

Now, I will say these good things first. The restaurant is beautifully decorated and they have a menu that has a host of variety and tastiness. It was a good start.  The waiter was funny and the hostess was prompt. Restaurants, however should be graded on the food and service, which is more like 90% of how I look at dining. It doesn't matter to me if your restaurant is a run-down shack, but if your food is on point, trust me, you'll win my praise.

My party arrived during non-peak hours and was quickly seated. We were all ready to enjoy some delicious fusion. We ordered, enjoyed some funny puns from our waiter, and he told us, twenty minutes--fine that's typical. We listened to reggae, odd choice for a hip-restaurant. Why have it on blast and on repeat? Something wasn't quite right with the ambiance.

Half an hour in: It was noticeable that the wait staff began to ignore us. One of my friends had his hand in the air for five minutes, trying to ask where the food was.

One hour later, our first bowl of pho hits the table. It's cold. The Butcher's Bowl is sparse--for being called the Butcher there seemed to be a lack of meat. I don't suppose the Butcher had to run out and catch it himself. Anyway, the flavor of the pho was different--probably would have tasted amazing had it been served fresh rather than left out to cool, or microwave--whichever the case. As it was, cold, made it a disappointment.

The crab eggrolls came out at the 1:20 mark. Burnt. Black. extra chewy. Ate it anyway, because: hangry.

The check came. My friend put down his credit card, and not a moment later was the card picked up. Service goes fast when you're taking payment from a customer.

Wait staff had the nerve to come back and say, "thanks for coming! sorry about your experience, please come back and I hope it'll turn out better!" All the while offering no way to make peace or win back our patronage.

Don't believe the hype. Overpriced. Bad service. Forgettable food. Check out some of the authentic pho places in Torrance or even one of the smaller ma & pop shops on Culver blvd.</review>

<user>115968246354963955827< /user><user_name>Michelle Yenter< /user_name><Time>1605239739280</Time><Rating>3</Rating><review>It's OK, but could improve. You walk in and the place doesn't even look like a restaurant; all I see are children's toys and disheveled employees, so the welcome and entrance isn't very welcoming. The meat is spot-on (we tried filet mignon and chicken) and the teas are delicious. However, the bowls are part of the pho experience- they are too deep/narrow here and need to be shallow and wider with MORE broth to allow the vegetables and meat to cook. They give you so many delicious vegetables, but not enough room in the bowl or broth to enjoy them. The broth was also on the sweet side, I couldn't place it but there was a spice that shouldn't be in it. Normally I enjoy sipping the broth after, but I didn't enjoy it. Finally, the hand-written menus on laminated cardboard are unimpressive, especially after the unimpressive welcome. This place could be amazing if just a few things were different!</review>< pics>

<UserId.>117929628493522303460< /UserId.><username>Amesia X<//username>< date>

<rate>5<//rate>< review>
This is my 5th visit and I'm finally posting because I don't want this place to go anywhere.  This place is a true gem hidden within a nondescript plaza (and without signage) so I've missed the entrance twice.  In my life, I've eaten countless homemade pho, cooked pho myself, and frequented hundreds of pho restaurants.  This place is legitimate.  While Santa Monica and West LA is generally a desert for quality pho, Camp Pho stands out and ranks among the best pho restaurants I've had.  Pho purists may complain about the price (~$12 for a small pho bowl) but it's Venice so priced accordingly to the local market.  For for timers, I recommend the large butcher pho bowl with a side of Hanoi crab egg rolls and a Thai iced tea.<//review>

<UserId.>114861004532389296064<//UserId.>< Name>
Jason Harrold<//Name>
<Date>1547166620842< /Date><rating>2<//rating><text>BYOC- Bring your own chopsticks.

I wanted to try Camp Pho as it was a new spot that opened up a few months ago.  I have walked by a few times and am always open to tasting new places.

The place was PACKED at 830pm. I checked over the menu and spotted some new things I wanted to try, looked at the reviews and they seemed good.

The service was slow and the night started to feel like the place has a few kinks to work out.  The table that we were sat at was not clean. there were several small dishes on the table, also not clean.  I noticed a few other things and decided to stop looking because this kind of thing starts to put me off about a place.  Dirty front of house generally means dirty back of house....Not a good first impression to say the least.

I asked the server for some suggestions from the menu and she said everything is good. Ok...

When it came time to order, the first two appetizers we ordered were sold out. So we didnt order another. The server made the suggestion to order the brisket Pho and when my gf ordered it the server back pedaled and said they were out of that as well.

Brisket is a tougher, less expensive cut from the others on the menu (filet mignon, ribeye), its also a pretty popular cut of meat for Pho so kinda surprised they were out but again the service is slow so might have helped if we knew that off the bat, probably something the staff should tell people when they hand them menus but Ok...  So the GF ordered a  Regular filet mignon Pho bowl and I ordered the large mixed meat  Pho bowl (Brisket which they were out of , Filet, ribeye and meatball) because, being it was our first time, I wanted to see the difference and taste several meats. I also opted out of having the Tripe.

The server boasted that the Pho was cooked 30 hours or something to that effect but it took a LONG TIME (which felt like 30hours) to get our food, or even the drinks that we ordered.

BIG PHO-BLEMO is that Meat quality here was sub par.  The meat balls have large, hard, rubbery pieces of gristle in them.  In fact, the meatball is a bit rubbery as well, the first bite was like chewing on a dog toy so I picked out "meatball" and placed it on the stack of dirty dishes that were still on our table when we arrived.  For a dish that has several meat cuts highlighted I couldn't distinguish between them.  Aside from the meat ball a filet should be distinguishable from a ribeye and they just tasted bland, not seasoned, over cooked and VERY dry.  How meat can be that dry sitting in a bowl of Pho is beyond me.

The reason that I say to bring your own chopsticks is that they use very cheaply made plastic chopsticks which are not conducive to gripping the noodles to eat them neatly, your noodles will most certainly slip and splosh unless you can slurp them up fast.

The broth was good, the side of sprouts, mint, jalapeno and lime were standard but they sat under the bowl of pho.
The soup did stay warm the entire meal which is a testament to the bowl quality, I just wish that they took time to select better meat to go with the nice bowl. The meat quality was truly a major disappointment.
There are a lot of really great reviews on here about this place. It is cool that there is another soup spot on the westside, the broth is nice and the people there seem nice as well, its just a shame that the place wasnt run a bit better last night and that the meat quality was poor.
The place has potential and is in a great location.  I would only recommend that the place be kept a bit cleaner, the staff would communicate a bit more about what they were serving and a "your food will be out soon" and that maybe the chef could provide a better quality of meat.  I dont mind paying a bit more for better quality but when I order the dish and the meat is that bad, it would turn people off from giving it another shot.  That said, theres a lot of very positive reviews, mine is only one couples experience on one night.<//text>< Pictures>
None</Pictures>

<Time>1581580189829< /Time><Rate>4<//Rate>< review>
A great local dive bar with a chill atmosphere.  There are darts, pool tables, and a juke box - what more can you ask for?!  The staff here is pretty chill and friendly.  They have a decent selection of beer on tap as well as daily drink specials.  The prices are pretty reasonable.
There's also a few TVs if you want to catch a game or two.  As for parking, you should be able to find spots on the streets and a small lot next to the bar.  They don't have food here, but you're able to bring outside food in.</review>

< Review>
My friend and I go here often to pass time while our kids are in classes. We love it. The bartenders are always nice and remembered us after the very first time we walked in. It's quite tropic inside and they're specialty drinks make you feel like you're in Hawaii. The mojito is amazing with coconut and mint. They are not heavy in the alcohol but the pina coladas are pre mixed and that seems to be the strongest drink. They have an outside patio for smokers or people that want to feel the air while they're drinking. Seems like a lot of "studio" people hang out there after work. Happy hour ends at 7 so make sure you get there before then. We've come in close to seven and purchased 2 drinks and they held it the second one for us at the Happy hour price. I highly recommend this place. Parking is only street parking but I've never had any issue finding a spot.<//Review>

< name>
Christopher Brown< /name>
< review>
Los Angeles has so many beautiful and iconic bars and lounges throughout its wonderful borders. No matter what your tastes are there is at least a dozen or so watering holes to wet your thirst and fit your vibe. Unfortunately, The Falls isn't one of them.

Located in the heart of downtown L.A. this place was absolutely a cluster of mismatched ideas and wrong thoughts. The moist poignant of them would have to be the set the DJ played for where not only my party but the crowd around me were commenting on the awfulness of the music selection. It would switch from music you would hear from Mornings Become Eclectic (but the nightmare version) to a club banger to industrial music with no beat or bearing. It was so jarring that even with the drinks (and they do make good ones) be drank it was hard to enjoy the atmosphere, which is a damn shame because the deco is modern, although a bit mismatched with art deco and lumberjack designs placed side-by-side as well. Many would consider this to be a bar that matches the taste of the movement of Los Angeles these days but experiencing it myself I couldn't help but feel like it was utter crap.

Perhaps it was an off night, and I really want that to be the reason, because the reviews here are so high and some of my fellow Yelpers I follow love this place. So if I do return here I hope I never come back with the same DJ again.

The Breakdown

Pros
- creative drinks
- interesting architecture
- great location in the heart of Downtown Los Angeles
- lenient dress code

Cons
- awful, AWFUL music that can ruin an entire night and make you say, "I. Literally. Can't. Even."< /review>

<username>Esther Kim<//username><date>1446965460975<//date><Rating>3</Rating><text>A couple of friends and I came here for happy hour one weekend. Their happy hour is every day (including weekends) from 5-9PM which is pretty nice.

They have three cocktails on their happy hour menu for $7 each... so we ordered all three:
-- The Hunter: Old Forester bourbon, fresh lemon and orange juice, honey, dash orange bitters on the rocks
-- Falls Royale: vodka or gin, fresh blood orange juice, simple syrup, champagne
-- The Rustic: Hendrick's gin, fresh grapefruit juice, fresh lemon juice, agave nectar, tonic on the rocks

I don't think any of them was bad, but I preferred the Falls Royale to the other two. You can choose vodka or gin for that cocktail so I went with vodka. I think it was a good choice :)

During happy hour they also offer $5 well drinks, $4 beer, and $6 beer and a shot. After we finished our three cocktails, one friend ordered a glass of Prosecco and we also got the $6 beer and shot. Gotta take advantage of those HH prices ;)

The Falls is pretty small and seating is really limited. We had to stand around the bar for a while before we were able to sit down. The bartender was nice but we didn't talk with him very much. Overall this is a chill place to grab a couple of drinks with friends, especially if it happens to be HH. Just be warned that it can get crowded quite easily.</text>< Pics>

< Text>
There is something relaxing in eating food with your hands. Of course you're not using bare have, but most of the Ethiopian dishes come with injera, a thin crepe-like flatbread, that can be used to grab and wrap small bites. Ethiopian dishes are often hot and always spicy. For instance, kitfo is similar to a steak tartare served with cottage cheese and vegetables. The restaurant is not particularly exotic and, if you're looking for the full Ethiopian experience, that might let you down, but the food is amazing and definitely worth a try. An interesting deviation from the usual dinner</Text>

<Response>None</Response>< review>
The food at Caf√© Ethiopia is good.  I ordered the veggie combo (carrots, potatoes, cabbage, yellow split peas, and spicy lentils) and ate the entire thing.  The portion size is smaller from the other Ethiopian/Eritrean places I've dined in, but the price is reflective.  It was about $1-$2 cheaper here.

The d√©cor and atmosphere are minimal.  They focus everything on the food, I suppose.  The waitress was friendly and attentive.

The only issue I had was the cleanliness of the bathroom.  I wash my hands before every meal, especially if I'm eating Ethiopian food.  It wasn't the cleanest, and it was very, very small.  The trash can is literally right in front of your face.. Maybe if I was taller it wouldn't have felt so close.

It' the only Ethiopian restaurant in the Mission.  It's worth a try if that's what you're craving.</review>

<Rate>5</Rate>< text>
Despite the fact it is a nondescript strip mall off of a Chevron station, this is a gem of a restaurant. Starting with the fresh salsa bar, then a taste of fresh juice, and finally I had two amazing fried cod tacos.

The servers were very helpful and nice. This is worth a trip up the 5 freeway to taste fresh seafood, new American style dishes, and awesome Latin plates. I want to try some of the pasta dishes and I really want to check out their breakfast offerings. Check this place out!</text>

Really good food! The black beans are delicious. The pinto beans are perfectly spicy. There's a sweet salsa I've never had ever & it's one of my favorites. The flavorful barbacoa tacos have as much meat as any burrito I've had before. The fresh chicken quesadillas, the organic kale & spinach smoothies made right in front of you, the cucumber lemonade... Just go already! You'll see me there for sure.<//text>

<Review>2020.03 - Update
I wish Google had an "update review" or "post another recent review" option - it would make life easier! Well, this place is great for some seafood! Staff is still awesome and food is still consistently cooked well! The pricing to portions after the six years of visiting this joint is still great! Overall a great one for a truly hidden gem! Their house salsa is addicting. Do not overeat and fill up with chips! Lol üòÇ It's the red, slightly thick, lightly sweet and shiny looking salsa. They need to sell gallons of it because I'd buy it! Definitely stop in for some killer stuff. Takeout is excellent, too!

Park at McDonald's (plenty of parking) and walk around or on the street if you can't find a spot in the tiny shopping center lot. It's at a gas station attached to a 7-11 on a busy intersection so parking goes quick.

A year ago: Love the staff here! They're always so pleasant! The food here is delicious! We frequent RJM for our company lunches! All the seafood dishes here are definitely a must try! Especially the Ahi Tuna Salad. The tuna is always made to perfection! The prices and portions are reasonable, too. I only need two tacos! If you're really hungry, three is perfect but you will be stuffed! Their complimentary salsa bar is fantastic! Their red salsa is....addicting. I can't say enough about this place because the staff also makes every visit enjoyable! It's connected to a gas station so the only problem is parking! <text>First of all, the parking sucks but don't let that deter you. Second of all, if you're in a hurry or do not have patience, then this is not the place for you. Your food is not ready to be served when you walk in, you will have to wait.

The staff is super friendly and welcoming. When they bring you chips, feel free to go to the salsa bar, their salsa game is strong.

This is our second time here. My wife ordered and loved her strawberry French toast. I had the Angus steak taco, which I enjoyed. I would love to have one with just steak, a fried egg and some salsa, but I'm a simple person. I also had the carne asada and eggs. My food seemed to disappear. Everything is flavorful and well worth the wait.

As for the decor...listen, if you come here and you're more concerned with the decor than the food, honestly, find a nice chain restaurant to go to. I have been cooking professionally for more than half my life and places like this are few and far in between.<//text><GmapID>0x80c29440709d932f:0x83f644c6b9a35560<//GmapID>< user_id>

I seldom write reviews, however felt compelled to share mv view of Bubbles & Brew. Having the opportunity to experience a wide variety of food, beverages, and services from establishments all over the world for many years may provide a little context.  I‚Äôm often surprised when reading a review where people are frustrated with their experience, related to either the food or services and judge the overall establishment.  An employee may be having a bad day, a cook may be overwhelmed at the time, or the food may not meet your expectations every time, which is likely to happen in any service establishment at some point.  When an establishment is busy, service will be impacted, it‚Äôs common sense.  What I‚Äôve learned is we as consumers should take a moment to share this with management in a polite and professional manner if our food or service results a negative experience.  Most times, management will be appreciative and address the issue.   My wife and I have been visiting Bubbles for years, and have become repeat customers based on their delicious food, wine options, and pleasant service.  Not much of a beer enthusiast so unable to provide input with regards to the beer selection.  We like the option to sit on the patio, indoors, or in the garden, based on who we‚Äôre with and weather.  If you're looking for a unique relaxing experience with delicious food you will not be disappointed with your visit to Bubbles.  I bring friends, family, and business professionals to Bubbles and the feedback has been consistent, positive and memorable.  It‚Äôs also the reason we frequent this establishment.< /Review>

<username>Darien Guy<//username>< text>
Bubbles is basically a spot where you can try some different wines and have a snack if you're feeling hungry. The menu is pretty much limited to meats and cheeses and flatbread pizzas. You're not going to get a full meal but you can get small bites.

You can choose from glasses or bottles of wine or some pretty interesting flights. I decided to try their wines of South Africa flight. Unfortunately I didn't like any of the 3 wines offered. They all smelled and tasted a bit weird. But the server was accommodating and let me try a glass of Zinfandel instead that was much better.

If you're looking for a place where you can try a new wine and have a quick bite to eat in a laid back atmosphere, then Bubbles is for you.</text>
